Now on a mammoth 35,000km walk, he couldn&#x27;t skip Australia which he had already visited many years ago."/><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://images.sbs.com.au/dims4/default/db7d559/2147483647/strip/true/crop/3024x1701+0+541/resize/1280x720!/quality/90/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fsbs-au-brightspot.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fa2%2F44%2F6fd26b944ee1ab156b8c1a38828d%2F10-uluru.jpg"/><meta name="twitter:url" content="https://www.sbs.com.au/language/italian/en/article/i-promised-uluru-id-be-back-says-italian-whos-been-walking-across-continents-for-four-years/kr3yxuf2q"/><script type="application/ld+json" data-testid="product-jsonld">{"@context":"https://schema.org","@graph":[{"@type":"Organization","name":"SBS Language","url":"https://phoenix.prod.edsprd01.aws.sbs.com.au/language","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","url":"https://www.sbs.com.au/_next/static/img/language/schema-logo-e7cccfe.png","width":"144","height":"144"}},{"@type":"Article","articleBody":"Nicol&amp;#xF2; Guarrera, aka &amp;#x2018;Pieroad&amp;#x2019; (p&amp;#xEC;e is Venetian for foot), is a man on a mission. Right now, he is walking from Alice Springs to Darwin, a distance of nearly 3,000km. But his plan is bigger, much bigger: he is travelling the world on foot. However, he isn&amp;apos;t campaigning for any cause. The walk is the cause. The 27-year-old  has already walked through Europe and South America and will enter Asia from Darwin where he reached via Adelaide &amp;#x2014; the two far ends of Australia. By the time you read this, he would have walked through three continents and ready for the fourth, covering approximately 35,000km. That makes four years of constant walking. It was May 2020, and the world was facing the COVID-19 pandemic. Nicol&amp;#xF2;, a 27-year-old man from Malo, a little Veneto village on the outskirts of Vicenza in Italy, worked for a chocolate brand as a category planner. One day, he left everything behind and began a world tour on foot. Let&amp;#x2019;s put this into numbers. For everyone who aims for the canonical 10,000 steps a day for their fitness, Nicol&amp;#xF2; will clock &amp;#x2013; considering an average of 1,350 steps per km &amp;#x2013; over 47 million steps by the end of his journey.  Nicol&amp;#xF2; is planning to end his journey in mid-2025, when he says, &amp;quot;I will walk back to my couch, at home.&amp;quot; That stacks up to 4,725 days or 13 years of walking. Nicol&amp;#xF2; is not alone on this mammoth mission. With every step he takes, his friend Ezio accompanies him. Ezio is not a fellow Italian walker, but a trolley in which Nicol&amp;#xF2; carries everything he needs to survive the trudge.  As with his job, he had to deal with logistics and problem-solving in this pursuit too, for which Nicol&amp;#xF2; says he adopted a very rational approach to the crucial phase of trip planning. He says he saved as much money as possible while planning the finest details of the trip like his itinerary, resting areas, food and other supplies. Then some sponsors followed, providing him with necessities such as shoes. &amp;#x201C;I have already gone through 14 pairs,&amp;quot; he laughs. Nicol&amp;#xF2; built his image through his walk, and sponsors began to walk with him.  &amp;quot;I don&amp;apos;t ask for money, I just want shoes or equipment. I have noticed that all my sponsors immediately felt empathetic towards my story, and they accepted to be a part of it,&amp;quot; he says. In the first two-and-a-half years, Nicol&amp;#xF2; crossed the border with France, then Spain. The second continent on his list was South America. Everything he does has &amp;#x201C;a strong rationale and follows a strict plan,&amp;#x201D; he says. The Italian walker is attracting supporters and social media followers day after day.  At the time writing this story, Nicol&amp;#xF2;, or Pieroad, had more than 22,000 followers on Instagram and almost 35,000 on TikTok.  Pieroad also has  website , where supporters can track Nicol&amp;#xF2; realtime and support him financially. His walks take him to remote places where he can go without a basic necessity of modern-day life for days on end: the internet.  Nicol&amp;#xF2; has his mobile phone, but he doesn&amp;apos;t mind being disconnected for a few days. &amp;quot;When I have connectivity, I get in touch with my dear ones and update my social media,&amp;quot; he adds. His daily routine is rigid and strategic.  &amp;quot;I wake up early, at around 6am and try to complete nearly 60 per cent of my daily target of 30-50 km in the morning,&amp;quot; Nicol&amp;#xF2; says. &amp;quot;If I sleep in the wild, I aim to wind everything up by around 5pm, because when the sun goes down, it gets pitch dark,&amp;quot; he adds. Setting up the tent, cooking some dinner, reading a book, writing some notes and absorbing his daily intake of thoughts, possibly admiring a starry nightsky, are the key-points of his afternoons and nights. &amp;quot;Unless I am with someone, in that case, I chat, chat, chat,&amp;quot; Nicol&amp;#xF2; says. To plan his diet, Nicol&amp;#xF2; needs to consider the limitations of space and time. He can&amp;#x2019;t store too much in Ezio and needs food that lasts at least four or five days. &amp;#x201C;This means lots of protein and chocolate, which gives me immediate energy. When I reach a village or town, I can eat everything I want, mainly chips,&amp;#x201D; he says. In Australia, &amp;#x201C;as the post works very well&amp;#x201D;, Nicol&amp;#xF2; prepared many small boxes while he was in Adelaide and posted them to the post offices he was meant to cross on his way across the length of the continent. &amp;quot;It always feels like finding a $50 note in an old pair of trousers, I always forget what I put in the boxes, and I feel overwhelmed by the good vibes that come out of these boxes,&amp;quot; he says with delight. Nicol&amp;#xF2; eats &amp;quot;like a cow&amp;quot;, as he needs energy for his mission. Lots of fats, no regrets. &amp;#x201C;Bread, chocolate, butter, jam. And water, of course. Plenty of water, either directly or through the incredible amount of fruit and veggies that I eat,&amp;quot; he tells SBS Italian. &amp;quot;In the desert, I lost seven kilos, I need to look after myself,&amp;quot; he adds. When he cooks his meals, Nicol&amp;#xF2; opts for carbs like pasta. He is Italian, after all.  Rice and proteins like canned legumes and &amp;quot;good fats&amp;quot; like avocado also make their way to his plate while he is on the move.  After walking through Ecuador, Peru and Chile, Nicol&amp;#xF2; landed in Sydney in March. With Ezio, of course. But why Australia? Nicol&amp;#xF2;&amp;#x2019;s fascinating mission may seem like the ideal life to some: full-time tourist, no limitations, no borders. Freedom at its best, people might think. But it&amp;#x2019;s not all that straightforward. Physical and mental health need to be handled with absolute care and attention in the terrain he traverses. &amp;#x201C;I must complete my Australian walk before the end of September as my visa will expire by then. And I am pushing to remain within this timeframe,&amp;#x201D; says Nicol&amp;#xF2;. Straight after finishing his walk through Sydney, Nicol&amp;#xF2; had the most challenging time. The rain did not give him a break and his mental health was impacted. &amp;quot;I kept repeating to myself, &amp;#x2018;why am I here? Why didn&amp;#x2019;t I stay in Chile, my favourite place&amp;apos;,&amp;quot; he says. Loneliness and silence, according to Nicol&amp;#xF2;, are &amp;#x201C;an absolute bliss&amp;#x201D; most of the time. &amp;#x201C;The connection between myself and why and what I am doing is profound,&amp;quot; he says. After Australia, Nicol&amp;#xF2; will fly to Kolkata, India. And from there, he will head northwest along River Ganga up to New Delhi. His way home will now need to be amended, as when he first planned the trip, Ukraine and Russia were not fighting a war. Finally, he is grateful to Australia. &amp;#x201C;The people are so kind and hospitable. I have been invited to their homes many times, and for me, it is something priceless, not only because I have the chance to talk to someone, but I can do my laundry and dry my clothes,&amp;#x201D; Nicol&amp;#xF2; signs off. &lt;b&gt;SBS Italian &lt;/b&gt; &lt;b&gt;Facebook&lt;/b&gt; &lt;b&gt;Twitter&lt;/b&gt; &lt;b&gt;Instagram &lt;/b&gt; &lt;b&gt;here&lt;/b&gt;","publisher":{"@type":"Organization","name":"SBS Language","url":"https://phoenix.prod.edsprd01.aws.sbs.com.au/language","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","url":"https://www.sbs.com.au/_next/static/img/language/schema-logo-e7cccfe.png","width":"144","height":"144"}},"author":[{"@type":"Person","name":"Andrea Pagani"}],"articleSection":"","url":"https://phoenix.prod.edsprd01.aws.sbs.com.au/language/italian/en/article/nicolo-is-walking-the-world-australia-i-love-you/kr3yxuf2q","datePublished":"2023-08-25T02:52:09.649Z","description":"Nicolò Guarrera aka &apos;Pieroad,&apos; quit his job one day in Italy and decided to see the world — on foot. Now on a mammoth 35,000km walk, he couldn&apos;t skip Australia which he had already visited many years ago.","dateCreated":"2023-08-25T02:52:09.649Z","dateModified":"2023-08-25T04:50:11.402Z","thumbnailUrl":"https://images.sbs.com.au/dims4/default/db7d559/2147483647/strip/true/crop/3024x1701+0+541/resize/1280x720!/quality/90/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fsbs-au-brightspot.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fa2%2F44%2F6fd26b944ee1ab156b8c1a38828d%2F10-uluru.jpg","headline":"‘I itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></p></div></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-1expiat"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-body1 css-wfd3rt" id="article-body" data-layer-event-source-global="‘I promised Uluru I’d be back,’ says Italian who&#x27;s been walking across continents for four years"><div class="MuiBox-root css-sxe9aa"><h6 class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-1lqews1">Key Points</h6><ul class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-body1 highlights css-1ra8xe3"><li class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle1 css-lm2zn4">Italian Nicolò Guarrera is walking across the world on foot.</li><li class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle1 css-lm2zn4">After Europe, South America and Australia, he will walk back home via India.</li><li class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle1 css-lm2zn4">He cooks and sleeps in the wild, asks for water from passersby, washes his clothes in houses of strangers.</li></ul></div><div><span>Nicol&#xF2; Guarrera, aka &#x2018;Pieroad&#x2019; (p&#xEC;e is Venetian for foot), is a man on a mission.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Right now, he is walking from Alice Springs to Darwin, a distance of nearly 3,000km.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>But his plan is bigger, much bigger: he is travelling the world on foot.</span><br/><br/></div><div class="css-1v0kanf"><div class="MuiGrid-root MuiGrid-container MuiGrid-direction-xs-column css-i2ezv1"></div></div><div><span>However, he isn&apos;t campaigning for any cause. The walk is the cause.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-gv60gm"><div class="fb-video" data-href="https://fb.watch/mCC3s4HA9w/" data-show-text="true" data-lazy="true" data-testid="embedded-facebook-video"></div></div><div><span>The 27-year-old  has already walked through Europe and South America and will enter Asia from Darwin where he reached via Adelaide &#x2014; the two far ends of Australia.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>By the time you read this, he would have walked through three continents and ready for the fourth, covering approximately 35,000km.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>That makes four years of constant walking.</span><br/></div><div></div><div><b><span>Wait, what? Let&#x2019;s contextualise.</span></b><br/><br/></div><div><span>It was May 2020, and the world was facing the COVID-19 pandemic.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Nicol&#xF2;, a 27-year-old man from Malo, a little Veneto village on the outskirts of Vicenza in Italy, worked for a chocolate brand as a category planner.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>One day, he left everything behind and began a world tour on foot.</span><br/></div><div></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">I thought that if beauty will save the world, as they say, who will save beauty? So, I decided to store as much beauty as possible, and because I always loved walking, I started planning this journey.</div><cite class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-c0aff">Nicolò Guarrera</cite></blockquote></div><div><span>Let&#x2019;s put this into numbers.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>For everyone who aims for the canonical 10,000 steps a day for their fitness, Nicol&#xF2; will clock &#x2013; considering an average of 1,350 steps per km &#x2013; over 47 million steps by the end of his journey. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Nicol&#xF2; is planning to end his journey in mid-2025, when he says, &quot;I will walk back to my couch, at home.&quot;</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>That stacks up to 4,725 days or 13 years of walking.</span><br/><br/></div><div><b><span>Find a friend, find a treasure</span></b><br/></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="5" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="PIEROAD 3" sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" srcSet="https://images.sbs.com.au/b1/86/538fabf7400682072fe27ed64ae4/3-hi-vi-world-wide-walk.JPG?imwidth=320 320w, https://images.sbs.com.au/b1/86/538fabf7400682072fe27ed64ae4/3-hi-vi-world-wide-walk.JPG?imwidth=360 360w, https://images.sbs.com.au/b1/86/538fabf7400682072fe27ed64ae4/3-hi-vi-world-wide-walk.JPG?imwidth=600 600w, https://images.sbs.com.au/b1/86/538fabf7400682072fe27ed64ae4/3-hi-vi-world-wide-walk.JPG?imwidth=960 960w, https://images.sbs.com.au/b1/86/538fabf7400682072fe27ed64ae4/3-hi-vi-world-wide-walk.JPG?imwidth=1280 1280w" src="https://images.sbs.com.au/b1/86/538fabf7400682072fe27ed64ae4/3-hi-vi-world-wide-walk.JPG?imwidth=1280" width="4032" height="3024" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Nicolò Guarrera pushing his trolley named Ezio along the road.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="PIEROAD 3"/><meta itemProp="width" content="4032"/><meta itemProp="height" content="3024"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="5"/></div></div><span>Nicol&#xF2; is not alone on this mammoth mission.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>With every step he takes, his friend Ezio accompanies him.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Ezio is not a fellow Italian walker, but a trolley in which Nicol&#xF2; carries everything he needs to survive the trudge. </span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">Ezio is the best companion. He helps immensely, he does not talk, and he listens. What more can you want?</div></blockquote></div><div><span>As with his job, he had to deal with logistics and problem-solving in this pursuit too, for which Nicol&#xF2; says he adopted a very rational approach to the crucial phase of trip planning.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>He says he saved as much money as possible while planning the finest details of the trip like his itinerary, resting areas, food and other supplies.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Then some sponsors followed, providing him with necessities such as shoes.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&#x201C;I have already gone through 14 pairs,&quot; he laughs.</span><br/></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="7" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="PIEROAD 13" sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" srcSet="https://images.sbs.com.au/07/43/1b970a0d437295a8f87a0ffb40be/img-20230725-wa0009.jpg?imwidth=320 320w, https://images.sbs.com.au/07/43/1b970a0d437295a8f87a0ffb40be/img-20230725-wa0009.jpg?imwidth=360 360w, https://images.sbs.com.au/07/43/1b970a0d437295a8f87a0ffb40be/img-20230725-wa0009.jpg?imwidth=600 600w, https://images.sbs.com.au/07/43/1b970a0d437295a8f87a0ffb40be/img-20230725-wa0009.jpg?imwidth=960 960w, https://images.sbs.com.au/07/43/1b970a0d437295a8f87a0ffb40be/img-20230725-wa0009.jpg?imwidth=1280 1280w" src="https://images.sbs.com.au/07/43/1b970a0d437295a8f87a0ffb40be/img-20230725-wa0009.jpg?imwidth=1280" width="1200" height="1600" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Somewhere between the earth and the sky is a stream of thoughts.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="PIEROAD 13"/><meta itemProp="width" content="1200"/><meta itemProp="height" content="1600"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="7"/></div></div><span>Nicol&#xF2; built his image through his walk, and sponsors began to walk with him. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&quot;I don&apos;t ask for money, I just want shoes or equipment. I have noticed that all my sponsors immediately felt empathetic towards my story, and they accepted to be a part of it,&quot; he says.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>In the first two-and-a-half years, Nicol&#xF2; crossed the border with France, then Spain.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>The second continent on his list was South America.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Everything he does has &#x201C;a strong rationale and follows a strict plan,&#x201D; he says.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">I need to walk at least 30km a day, and no more than 50km because my body needs sufficient rest. I can eat lots of fatty food; it serves my purpose.</div></blockquote></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="9" 35,000 on TikTok. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Pieroad also has </span><div class="MuiBox-root css-68lxg3" data-layer-event-source-placement="body" data-layer-event-source-title="embeded link" itemProp="height" content="4032"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="11"/></div></div><b><span>How does he survive?</span></b><br/><br/></div><div><span>His walks take him to remote places where he can go without a basic necessity of modern-day life for days on end: the internet. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Nicol&#xF2; has his mobile phone, but he doesn&apos;t mind being disconnected for a few days.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">It is a digital fasting that helps me detox, adds.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>His daily routine is rigid and strategic. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&quot;I wake up early, at around 6am and try to complete nearly 60 per cent of my daily target of 30-50 km in the morning,&quot; Nicol&#xF2; says.</span><br/></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="13" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="PIEROAD 6" sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" srcSet="https://images.sbs.com.au/fe/c9/fa9772214ac194b59c3b3353991a/7-in-tenda.jpg?imwidth=320 320w, https://images.sbs.com.au/fe/c9/fa9772214ac194b59c3b3353991a/7-in-tenda.jpg?imwidth=360 360w, https://images.sbs.com.au/fe/c9/fa9772214ac194b59c3b3353991a/7-in-tenda.jpg?imwidth=1280 1280w" src="https://images.sbs.com.au/fe/c9/fa9772214ac194b59c3b3353991a/7-in-tenda.jpg?imwidth=1280" width="3024" height="4032" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Nicolò Guarrera in his tent.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="PIEROAD 6"/><meta itemProp="width" content="3024"/><meta itemProp="height" content="4032"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="13"/></div></div><span>&quot;If I sleep in the wild, I aim to wind everything up by around 5pm, because when the sun goes down, it gets pitch dark,&quot; he adds.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Setting up the tent, cooking some dinner, reading a book, writing some notes and absorbing his daily intake of thoughts, possibly admiring a starry nightsky, are the key-points of his afternoons and nights.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&quot;Unless I am with someone, in that case, I chat, chat, chat,&quot; Nicol&#xF2; says.</span><br/></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="14" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="PIEROAD 8" sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" srcSet="https://images.sbs.com.au/c8/3e/c279484e4ac4b33294393c7aebff/9-campo-notturni.jpg?imwidth=320 320w, https://images.sbs.com.au/c8/3e/c279484e4ac4b33294393c7aebff/9-campo-notturni.jpg?imwidth=360 360w, https://images.sbs.com.au/c8/3e/c279484e4ac4b33294393c7aebff/9-campo-notturni.jpg?imwidth=600 600w, https://images.sbs.com.au/c8/3e/c279484e4ac4b33294393c7aebff/9-campo-notturni.jpg?imwidth=960 960w, https://images.sbs.com.au/c8/3e/c279484e4ac4b33294393c7aebff/9-campo-notturni.jpg?imwidth=1280 1280w" src="https://images.sbs.com.au/c8/3e/c279484e4ac4b33294393c7aebff/9-campo-notturni.jpg?imwidth=1280" width="3024" height="4032" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Under the Southern Cross.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="PIEROAD 8"/><meta itemProp="width" content="3024"/><meta itemProp="height" content="4032"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="14"/></div></div><span>To plan his diet, Nicol&#xF2; needs to consider the limitations of space and time.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>He can&#x2019;t store too much in Ezio and needs food that lasts at least four or five days.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&#x201C;This means lots of protein and chocolate, which gives me immediate energy. When I reach a village or town, I can eat everything I want, mainly chips,&#x201D; he says.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>In Australia, &#x201C;as the post works very well&#x201D;, Nicol&#xF2; prepared many small boxes while he was in Adelaide and posted them to the post offices he was meant to cross on his way across the length of the continent.</span><br/></div><div></div><div><span>&quot;It always feels like finding a $50 note in an old pair of trousers, I always forget what I put in the boxes, and I feel overwhelmed by the good vibes that come out of these boxes,&quot; he says with delight.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Nicol&#xF2; eats &quot;like a cow&quot;, as he needs energy for his mission. Lots of fats, no regrets.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&#x201C;Bread, chocolate, butter, jam. And water, of course. Plenty of water, either directly or through the incredible amount of fruit and veggies that I eat,&quot; he tells SBS Italian.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">Seriously, I eat double the amount I was used to, yet I am losing weight.</div></blockquote></div><div><span>&quot;In the desert, I lost seven kilos, I need to look after myself,&quot; he adds.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>When he cooks his meals, Nicol&#xF2; opts for carbs like pasta. He is Italian, after all. </span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Rice and proteins like canned legumes and &quot;good fats&quot; like avocado also make their way to his plate while he is on the move. </span><br/></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="17" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="Pieroad&#x27;s Diet.jpg" sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" width="1069" height="1865" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Nicolò&#x27;s diet in the desert.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="Pieroad&#x27;s Diet.jpg"/><meta itemProp="width" content="1069"/><meta itemProp="height" content="1865"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="17"/></div></div><b><span>Beneath the Southern Cross</span></b><br/><br/></div><div><span>After walking through Ecuador, Peru and Chile, Nicol&#xF2; landed in Sydney in March.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>With Ezio, of course.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>But why Australia?</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">I had travelled to Australia seven years ago and had such a magical moment watching Uluru that I promised I would return, so here I am.</div></blockquote></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="19" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="PIEROAD 12" sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" srcSet="https://images.sbs.com.au/60/18/1079670c4f9e98b4197956a7e80e/14-kings-canyon.jpg?imwidth=320 320w, https://images.sbs.com.au/60/18/1079670c4f9e98b4197956a7e80e/14-kings-canyon.jpg?imwidth=360 360w, https://images.sbs.com.au/60/18/1079670c4f9e98b4197956a7e80e/14-kings-canyon.jpg?imwidth=600 600w, style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">Nicolò Guarrera traverses the rocky terrain of northern Australia<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="PIEROAD 12"/><meta itemProp="width" content="3024"/><meta itemProp="height" content="4032"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="19"/></div></div><b><span>Not all that easy</span></b><br/><br/></div><div><span>Nicol&#xF2;&#x2019;s fascinating mission may seem like the ideal life to some: full-time tourist, no limitations, no borders.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Freedom at its best, people might think.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>But it&#x2019;s not all that straightforward.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>Physical and mental health need to be handled with absolute care and attention in the terrain he traverses.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&#x201C;I must complete my Australian walk before the end of September as my visa will expire by then. And I am pushing to remain within this timeframe,&#x201D; says Nicol&#xF2;.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">I had an issue with knee bursitis in Chile, and I need to be very careful. But I also cannot afford to stop completely for a few days.</div></blockquote></div><div></div><div><span>Straight after finishing his walk through Sydney, Nicol&#xF2; had the most challenging time.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>The rain did not give him a break and his mental health was impacted.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&quot;I kept repeating to myself, &#x2018;why am I here? Why didn&#x2019;t I stay in Chile, my favourite place&apos;,&quot; he says.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">A part of me wanted to quit and being alone might be an impossible cliff to climb in those moments.</div></blockquote></div><div><span>Loneliness and silence, according to Nicol&#xF2;, are &#x201C;an absolute bliss&#x201D; most of the time.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&#x201C;The connection between myself and why and what I am doing is profound,&quot; he says.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">The slow pace of walking reflects another way of interpreting life; this is the best lesson I am learning.</div></blockquote></div><div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><div itemscope="" itemType="https://schema.org/ImageObject" id="24" data-testid="embeded-image"><div class="MuiBox-root css-14nolla"><img sx="[object Object]" alt="PIEROAD 11" sizes="(min-width:1440) 920px, (min-width:960px) 83vw, 100vw" srcSet="https://images.sbs.com.au/6b/bc/d07e3a8d46daa44570639d1828dc/12-outback.jpg?imwidth=320 320w, https://images.sbs.com.au/6b/bc/d07e3a8d46daa44570639d1828dc/12-outback.jpg?imwidth=360 360w, https://images.sbs.com.au/6b/bc/d07e3a8d46daa44570639d1828dc/12-outback.jpg?imwidth=600 600w, https://images.sbs.com.au/6b/bc/d07e3a8d46daa44570639d1828dc/12-outback.jpg?imwidth=960 960w, https://images.sbs.com.au/6b/bc/d07e3a8d46daa44570639d1828dc/12-outback.jpg?imwidth=1280 1280w" src="https://images.sbs.com.au/6b/bc/d07e3a8d46daa44570639d1828dc/12-outback.jpg?imwidth=1280" width="3024" height="4032" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="css-0" loading="lazy" style="color:transparent;width:100%;height:100%"/></div><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-subtitle2 css-h2a21c" data-testid="heroImageCaption">The world at his feet.<span itemProp="name" data-testid="leadImageSource"> Credit: <!-- -->Instagram/Pieroad__</span></div><meta itemProp="name" content="PIEROAD 11"/><meta itemProp="width" content="3024"/><meta itemProp="height" content="4032"/><meta itemProp="identifier" content="24"/></div></div><b><span>Maybe, tomorrow</span></b><br/><br/></div><div><span>After Australia, Nicol&#xF2; will fly to Kolkata, India.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>And from there, he will head northwest along River Ganga up to New Delhi.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>His way home will now need to be amended, as when he first planned the trip, Ukraine and Russia were not fighting a war.</span><br/></div><div class="MuiBox-root css-exul89"><blockquote class="css-1p6x4it"><div class="MuiTypography-root MuiTypography-h4 css-1aiu0h6">It will take me another couple of years to return home. Too late to ditch now!</div></blockquote></div><div><span>Finally, he is grateful to Australia.</span><br/><br/></div><div><span>&#x201C;The people are so kind and hospitable. I have been invited to their homes many times, and for me, it is something priceless, not only because I have the chance to talk to someone, but I can do my laundry and dry my clothes,&#x201D; Nicol&#xF2; signs off.</span><br/><br/><br/></div><div><b><span>Listen to&#xA0;</span></b><div class="MuiBox-root css-68lxg3" data-layer-event-source-placement="body"
